Jiang Zungui's Coffin Was Encoffined Yesterday 195

Jiang Boqi, the former Governor of Zhejiang and Guangdong Provinces, an advanced member of the Party and the State, passed away on the 5th. All sectors deeply mourned his death. The details have been published in yesterday's newspaper. Yesterday at 4:00 PM was the time for the encoffining ceremony. For a time, those who came to pay their respects filled the door, and they all personally offered the ceremony of encoffining. A huge mat awning was built on the lawn of Jiang's residence (No. 23 Sapo Road), and the plain colors fluttered, attracting the attention of passers-by. It is said that the funeral committee has been organized and established, and Li Liejun is the general manager. Therefore, he did not avoid the heat and personally went back and forth to command. Those who saw his old friendship and party spirit were moved. Xiong Shihui, Commander of the Songhu Garrison Command, who was in Jiangxi, specially sent his aide-de-camp Jiang Yi as a representative to take care of everything. The military band of the command arrived at the scene, all with black gauze wrapped around their arms, and respectfully played mourning music. Mayor Zhang Yuejun arrived at 7:00 AM. Among the friends were Xu Shiying, Zhang Zhijiang, Cheng Qian, Xu Qian, Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Zhou Fengqi, Chu Huiseng, Gao Zibai, Li Zhengwu, Tao Jiayao, Li Yujie, Shen Tianxin, and other representatives from all walks of life, totaling more than 200 people. Wang Jingwei, Tang Shaoyi, Sun Ke, Xu Chongzhi, and Gu Yingfen also sent condolences from Guangzhou and telegraphed 1,000 yuan each as a funeral gift. Jiang was a senior member of the Tongmenghui who destroyed his family to make a revolution and devoted himself to the party and the country. He was dignified, honest, and upright. Although he held important positions, his situation after his death was extremely desolate. The family members and the funeral committee plan to hold the funeral on the fifth seventh day and return to their hometown for burial. The All-Zhejiang Association believes that the Sangzi area has benefited and his legacy remains. It is said that they have telegraphed the Zhejiang Provincial Government to forward the request to the National Government for preferential commendation to show loyalty and sincerity.

Workers in the Letterpress Printing Industry Resumed Work Yesterday 196

Still Working Nine Hours Temporarily

Two thousand five hundred workers in more than 60 letterpress printing factories in Shanghai demanded that the capitalists implement the eight-hour work system and improve their treatment in accordance with the provisions of the Factory Law. After being idle for several days, the Social Affairs Bureau convened labor and management for negotiations. They resumed work yesterday, and the working hours are still the usual nine hours, from 8:00 AM to 6:00 PM, with one hour for lunch break. All issues related to treatment improvement will be discussed by the Social Affairs Bureau convening both parties on another day.

China Merchants Electric Power Company

Employee Request for Improved Benefits 197

The entire workforce of the China General Edison Company had previously proposed improvements to their benefits, which have now been satisfactorily resolved. The company's General Manager, Lu Bohong, subsequently issued a notice stating, in essence, that the company's newly revised worker benefits regulations are slightly more favorable than before and have been approved by the board of directors. As employees also serve the company, they cannot be excluded. The manager has decided to submit a request to the next board meeting to formulate separate employee benefits rules that will certainly not be inferior to those of the workers, in order to demonstrate impartiality and provide encouragement. Please be informed accordingly. It is now known that after General Manager Lu Bohong's announcement, all employees of the company immediately convened a general meeting and resolved to propose eight articles. Eleven representatives were elected to send a letter to the company authorities, setting a date for signing an agreement so that labor and management could jointly abide by it. After the employees sent three letters to the company requesting a joint discussion and signing, the company authorities delayed without responding. Consequently, all employees collectively decided to petition the Municipal Party Department and the Social Affairs Bureau for a swift resolution. The eight proposed improvements to benefits are listed below: (1) Request the company to increase employee benefits and establish fixed salary rates for each level to enhance work efficiency. Measures: (A) The minimum monthly salary for a section chief should not be less than 350 yuan, the minimum monthly salary for a deputy section chief should not be less than 300 yuan, the minimum monthly salary for a section staff member should not be less than 180 yuan, the minimum monthly salary for a team leader should not be less than 250 yuan, the minimum monthly salary for a team member should not be less than 140 yuan, and the minimum monthly salary for a trainee should not be less than 40 yuan. (B) Trainees should receive a salary increase once every year-end, with a minimum increase of 10 yuan. However, after three years of service, they should be promoted to team members and receive a team member's salary. (C) Whenever an employee is promoted, their job salary should increase according to their level. (D) For current company employees, the appropriate salary level should be determined as follows: Section chiefs and team leaders can receive salaries based on their title and level. For other section employees, three employees from each section should be publicly elected by the section, and with the approval of the employee representatives, they will work with the respective section chief to impartially determine the appropriate salary level for each employee. This will be reported to the employee representatives for approval and then communicated to the company for salary payment according to the level. (E) The current salary rates are tentatively set for a period of three years. After three years, due to the continued increase in the cost of living and the company's expanding business, employees may request the company authorities to modify and increase salaries according to the living situation. (2) Request the company to provide free electricity to employees for residential use. (3) The company should not suspend employees without a valid reason. If an employee has committed a serious offense that warrants suspension, the criminal act should be announced in detail. (4) When an employee retires, the company should provide a retirement gratuity based on their years of service, paying one month's salary for each year of service, with the salary at the time of retirement as the standard. Two months for two years, three months for three years, and so on. Months less than one year can be calculated based on the average distribution of twelve months of the year. (5) If an employee dies due to illness, the company should provide a one-time funeral expense of 1,000 yuan and a separate retirement gratuity based on the years of service, which should be fully received by the family. (6) Employees who work overtime on Sundays or holidays should be paid one-thirtieth of their monthly salary for each overtime session. (7) Employees receive an annual bonus of two months' salary at the end of each year. However, new employees who start service in July will only receive six-twelfths of the full annual bonus, and those who start service in December will only receive one-twelfth of the annual bonus. In the interest of fair treatment, whenever an employee resigns, the annual bonus should be divided into twelve parts, and the employee should be paid the corresponding number of twelfths based on the number of months they have served in the current year, in order to ensure fairness. (8) The company's Employees' Welfare Association is a place for employees to cultivate their minds, strengthen their bodies, and enjoy legitimate recreation. The company should subsidize the association's expenses with 600 yuan per month and provide a one-time allocation of 3,000 yuan for the association to purchase equipment.

World Liner

Replacing Workers Sparks Unrest 198

Peaceful Resolution Reached in Shanghai

The President Adams, a world liner of the Dollar Steamship Lines, arrived in Shanghai this time from New York, USA, and entered the port on the 3rd of this month. The ship was docked at the Bailianjing Wharf in Pudong. The stewards, servants, and other personnel on board became agitated upon learning that the foreman intended to replace them with new recruits. Fortunately, the Shanghai representative of the company, with the aim of resolving the matter peacefully, prevented any unexpected incidents from occurring. The details of the event are as follows:

Revision of Contract: The stewards, servants, and other personnel employed on the ship had previously entered into employment contracts in Singapore. Their salaries averaged 25 yuan per month, paid in Singapore currency. Upon the President Adams' arrival in Shanghai, the ship's foreman proposed that the workers' contracts be revised and signed in Shanghai, allowing payment in Shanghai currency, which would save the company a few yuan per month per person. The workers immediately expressed their opposition and, in addition to requesting Mr. Suckle, the shipowner's representative, to convey their concerns to the Shanghai office, they also telegraphed the head office in San Francisco for assistance.

Replacing Workers: The ship's foreman, determined to dismiss the sailors who resisted the contract revision, hired a new batch of workers, totaling more than 80, in Shanghai. The foreman led them onto the ship at 7 a.m. on the 5th. Upon the workers' arrival on board, the existing crew members united in resistance, guarding the gangway to prevent the foreman and the new workers from boarding. They also requested the American sailors on board to assist them in their struggle. The American stokers and other personnel expressed their sympathy for the veteran workers and drove the foreman ashore.

Request to the Shanghai Office: Taking advantage of this opportunity, the workers put forward their conditions for security: (1) The existing crew members on board must not be replaced. (2) The contracts must still be signed in Singapore, and the workers' salaries must be paid in Straits dollars. (3) The foreman's contracting system and deductions must be abolished. (4) Improvements in treatment, etc. Representatives were then elected by the workers to present their case to Mr. Suckle, the shipowner's representative, and to convey it to the Shanghai office. The Shanghai representative, recognizing that the fault lay with the foreman, immediately agreed to the sailors' requests and ordered them to resume work quickly.

Page 14

The new workers were withdrawn: The Shanghai office, recognizing that the ship was a regularly scheduled world liner and that any delay would be unacceptable, immediately ordered the foreman to dismiss the newly hired workers and prevent them from boarding. At the same time, the workers on board were instructed to resume work quickly. Cargo loading and passenger boarding proceeded as usual, and the ship departed from Shanghai on the morning of the 6th, returning directly to New York. The workers on board, grateful for the assistance of the American sailors on the ship in achieving this victory, expressed their deep appreciation. Representatives were dispatched by the workers to express their thanks and to request that American and Chinese sailors unite permanently in the future.

Request for Reconsideration

New Organizational Law of the Directorate General of Posts 199

Petition from the Postal Workers' Unions to Director Qian

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union and the Shanghai Postal Employees' Union jointly submitted a document to Director Qian, requesting reconsideration of the new organizational law of the Directorate General of Posts. The petition stated that the recently promulgated organizational law of the Directorate General of Posts, in consideration of the actual circumstances of the postal service, contains certain unsuitable provisions. They jointly requested, with utmost sincerity, that it be forwarded to the Ministry of Communications of the Executive Yuan, which would then request the Legislative Yuan to approve amendments to benefit communications and comply with public sentiment. It was noted that since its establishment, the Chinese postal service has undergone over thirty years of development, achieving remarkable results and consistently ranking as the leading state-owned enterprise. The primary reason for this success lies in the well-organized and systematic structure of the postal service, the relatively comprehensive existing regulations, the employees' reliance on guaranteed rights, and the resulting development of the business. However, the recently promulgated organizational law of the Directorate General of Posts introduces numerous changes to the existing system. Several aspects that are deemed incompatible with the circumstances of the postal service are listed below for consideration: (1) The position of Deputy Director General is not explicitly stipulated to be selected from experienced postal directors. It is recalled that when the right to manage the postal service was recovered, the former Director General, Mr. Meng Wangken, was promoted from his position as a senior postal director. At that time, the regulations of the Directorate General stipulated that the general managers should also be filled by personnel with experience in the postal service. This demonstrated the Minister's understanding of the difficulties involved in managing the postal service, which could not be easily handled by those unfamiliar with its operations. When the former Director General attended the Universal Postal Congress, the acting Director General, although not a postal service veteran, benefited from the assistance of several experienced managers, who provided support in managing the bureau's affairs. Fortunately, few obstacles were encountered. Therefore, the current regulations of the Directorate General still stipulate that the managers should be filled by personnel with experience in the postal service. The unions have repeatedly applied to the Ministry of Communications, the Bureau, and other higher-level authorities, requesting that this principle be retained when revising the organizational law of the postal service to benefit the communications industry. These requests were largely accepted. However, the Legislative Yuan's recent revision of the organizational law of the Directorate General of Posts changed the general managers to Director General and Deputy Director General. The qualifications for the appointment of the Deputy Director General omitted the provision that it should be filled by personnel with experience in the postal service, causing widespread anxiety among the staff. While the unions greatly admire the Director General's expertise in postal science, the position of Deputy Director General is also crucial. Ultimately, selecting someone familiar with the postal service would be more mutually beneficial. Furthermore, the unions especially hope that the position of Deputy Director General will be reserved for promotion from among postal directors, to provide encouragement and support. The current managers have already been appointed by the Ministry of Communications as Deputy Director General, demonstrating that the Minister still considers the previous regulations to be appropriate. It is therefore necessary to request the Legislative Yuan to approve an amendment that retains the qualification for the Deputy Director General of the Directorate General of Posts to be selected from experienced postal directors, thereby reassuring the public. (2) The Chief Secretary should also be explicitly designated to be appointed from senior postal personnel. According to the new organizational law, the Chief Secretary is equivalent to the Director of the Secretariat in the current regulations. The powers and responsibilities are similar. The Directors of the Secretariat, like other directors, have traditionally been filled by personnel with experience in the postal service. The new organizational law also stipulates that the Director and Deputy Director should be appointed from postal directors and deputy postal directors. Therefore, the same principle should apply to the Chief Secretary and should be explicitly stated. (3) The affairs of the Performance Evaluation and Auditing Departments should continue to be handled by the Bureau. The Performance Evaluation Department is responsible for matters related to the promotion, demotion, and dismissal of postal personnel. It has always been managed according to established regulations, guaranteeing the rights of tens of thousands of employees and consolidating the foundation of the postal service. The Auditing Department is responsible for auditing the national postal service's receipts and expenditures and supervising accounting. Its strictness has ensured the clarity of postal finances. The new organizational law does not provide for the establishment of these two departments, which must be assigned to other departments. If they are divided or separated from the Bureau's organization, the entire postal system and its structure will inevitably be disrupted. The theory is unsound, the facts are fraught with difficulties, and the resulting malpractices will cause widespread suspicion and fear, which is not beneficial to the communications industry. Therefore, these two departments should continue to be handled by the Bureau to maintain consistency and preserve the old regulations. In summary, the above three points are matters of concern for the future of the postal service and cannot be ignored. It is appropriate to submit this document for consideration and forward it to the Ministry of Communications of the Executive Yuan, requesting that the Legislative Yuan approve amendments to the organizational law of the Directorate General of Posts, which would be mutually beneficial to both the public and the postal service. Furthermore, the position of Postal Inspector, while important and appointed by the Ministry of Communications, is not explicitly stipulated in the new organizational law. It seems appropriate to request an amendment to include it. Respectfully submitted to Qian, Director General of the Directorate General of Posts, August 4th, 20th year of the Republic of China.

French Concession

Two Courts Officially Opened Yesterday 200

The newly established Higher and District Courts of China within the French Concession of this city, after taking over the French Public Concession on July 31, were established the following day. Due to the urgency of the time, the internal organization was not yet complete. Therefore, only yesterday, at 10:00 a.m., did they officially open and begin accepting new and old civil and criminal cases. However, the Third Branch of the Higher Court, because the original French Public Concession did not have an appeals mechanism, had no previous appeals cases to hear. New appeals cases have not yet been completed by the prosecutor. Therefore, the High Court will actually need several more days before it can officially open.

Case of Chinese Policeman Shot

Shanghai Municipal Council Attempts to Settle with Compensation 206

Decision to Send Another Letter for Serious Negotiations

The case of the Chinese policeman shot on Hart Road has not been resolved despite repeated negotiations by the Municipal Government with the Shanghai Municipal Council, due to the Council's persistent delays. According to information obtained from investigations by both the Shanghai Municipal Council and the Municipal Government, the Council, after receiving the Municipal Government's request for mediation, sent representatives to discuss the matter with the Municipal Government. They were willing to offer generous compensation to the injured policeman, but they still refused to admit fault or accept guarantees regarding the punishment of the assailant. As a result, the talks were inconclusive. The Municipal Government stated that it considered the case to be a whole incident, and that it was concerned with clarifying right and wrong and bringing the assailant to justice, not simply settling the matter with more money. If the purpose of the negotiations was solely for monetary compensation, the Municipal Government would not have bothered to handle the case. The case is of a criminal nature. If the criminal part is not resolved, the civil part cannot be discussed. It is regrettable that the Shanghai Municipal Council has misunderstood the objective and has not resolved the matter quickly and reasonably. Therefore, the Municipal Government has decided to send another letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council for serious negotiations and to urge a swift resolution and response.

New British Warship to Test Drive Tomorrow 207

A new British shallow-water gunboat, specially designed for the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, was built in China this year and commissioned to the Jiangnan Shipyard. The raw materials for the ship arrived in Shanghai in February of this year. The Jiangnan Shipyard dispatched personnel and accompanying staff to assemble the prefabricated materials according to the blueprints. The work took only five months. The ship is 158 feet long, 28 feet wide, and has a draft of 5 feet 9 inches, with a displacement of 450 tons. It has three gun emplacements, resembles a merchant ship, and has many rooms. The exterior is white and very beautiful. It is named Falcon. It is scheduled to be fully completed on the 20th of this month. Tomorrow (the 8th), it must first be test-driven in Longhua to check its speed.

Chinese and Foreign Joint Relief Society

Continues to Receive Relief Requests from Various Provinces 208

The Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Joint Relief Society received an urgent telegram from the Yexian County Flood Relief Committee in Henan Province: "Yexian County is unfortunate and has repeatedly suffered disasters. Calamities and disasters have occurred in succession, and the people cannot bear it. Unexpectedly, in June, another flood disaster occurred, destroying countless houses. Grain and livestock were washed away. Many of the good fields in the countryside were turned into gullies. Many people were injured or killed. Such a catastrophe is unprecedented in the past thirty years. The autumn harvest is now hopeless, and it is increasingly difficult to prepare for winter," etc. They also received a telegram from the Suiping County Relief Branch in Henan Province: "Since July 9th, heavy rain has fallen in Suiping County, without ceasing for days, causing mountain floods to erupt and the entire county to become a swamp. All crops were washed away, and more than twenty embankments collapsed. Many families lost all their members. Countless livestock were washed away. The estimated losses amount to tens of millions. Winter is approaching, and how will we survive? Under the threat of hunger and cold, taking risks is even more worrisome," etc. They also received a telegram from various institutions and groups in Gaochun County, Jiangsu Province: "Since the summer, the people of Chunyi have suffered from the backflow of the Yangtze River and the flooding of lakes. Furthermore, there has been continuous rain for ten days, causing mountain floods to erupt. As a result, dikes have collapsed, fields and crops have been flooded, houses have collapsed, and livestock have been swept away. In the entire territory, two hundred and twenty dikes have been submerged, with no fewer than one hundred and several tens of dikes having sunk one after another. Starving people are everywhere, and their cries shake the heavens. The tragic situation cannot be described in words," etc. They also received telegrams from the Chaoxian County Government and the Agricultural Association Red Cross in Anhui Province: "Chaoxian County has suffered from heavy rain for ten days, causing mountain floods to erupt. All dikes in the county have collapsed. Grain and goods have been swept away. The estimated losses are difficult to calculate. Currently, there are more than 100,000 people without food or shelter," etc. They also received a public letter from various institutions and groups in Guoyang County, Anhui Province: "Our county has suffered from repeated disasters in recent years. Unfortunately, in July of this year, there was continuous rain again, causing the rivers to burst and flood, inundating fields and houses, and scattering the people. The property losses are incalculable. Cultivation has been delayed, and the autumn harvest is hopeless. Now, there are starving people everywhere, crying for food. The sight is heartbreaking and unbearable," etc. They also received a telegram from Fengyang, Anhui: "The Huai River has flooded, inundating countless fields and houses. 100,000 disaster victims have no place to go and cannot get food," etc. They also received a telegram from various groups in Anhui Qiu: "Heavy rain has been falling continuously, and mountain floods and river tides have increased, creating a vast expanse of water. People, livestock, and fields have been submerged. The autumn harvest is hopeless, and the people are anxiously awaiting food," etc. They also received a telegram from the Wuxing County Flood Relief Committee in Zhejiang Province: "Continuous rain has caused a disaster, and the four rural areas have become a swamp. The disaster is extremely severe, and the autumn harvest is hopeless," etc. They also received a telegram from the Hunan Xiang Flood Relief Association: "Hunan Province has suffered from repeated military conflicts and bandits in recent years. The people are dying and lying on pillows, a tragic sight beyond description. However, since the beginning of this summer, there has been continuous rain, causing mountain floods to erupt. Fields, houses, people, livestock, and property have been washed away in countless quantities. Deaths are recorded on the roads, and cries shake the heavens. The losses have already reached tens of millions of yuan, and the number of casualties has reached hundreds of thousands. The autumn harvest is hopeless, and there is no livelihood," etc.

Begging for Relief for the Flood in Northern Anhui 209

Letters and Telegrams Received by the Jisheng Society

The Chinese Jisheng Society recently received a telegram forwarded by the society's committee member, Mr. Ding Junjiahou, from the Anhui Provincial Charity Federation, stating: "The Anhui Province has been flooded due to continuous rain for a long time, turning cities into swamps. The Guangji Embankment, which is the lifeline for the people's food supply in the provincial capital, collapsed on You Day, causing countless deaths and drownings. It is a tragic situation beyond description. Emergency relief is being distributed in various ways. Please grant a large sum of money to save the hungry and drowning, and please reply by telegram," etc. They also received a telegram from the Guangji Embankment Flood Relief Association, stating that the collapse of the Guangji Embankment has left more than 200,000 disaster victims waiting to be rescued and urging urgent relief. They are eagerly awaiting orders, etc. Furthermore, more than 100 zhang of the northwest embankment of the Guangcheng Embankment collapsed and washed away due to failure to rescue it in time. Countless people and livestock were drowned and washed away. Representative Xu Pingxuan came to the association with mail and telegrams to request relief. In addition, Zhai Zhancheng, director of flood relief at the Wuhu branch of the association, reported that the Mahu Fenglin Shanrui Embankment and the smaller embankments in Wuhu were almost entirely destroyed. The embankments that have not been breached are in imminent danger. The streets and roads are several feet deep in water. The affected farmers are bringing their elderly and children into the city to take shelter in temples and on the embankments, exposed to the wind and rain and unable to get a full meal all day. Their homes have been flooded, and their belongings have been lost. The sorrowful and tragic situation is indescribable. The Jinbaoren Embankment in the northern rural area of Xuan County, the Xihang West River Embankment in the western rural area, and the Taifeng Embankment and Lingdu Embankment in Nanling have all collapsed, resulting in hundreds of deaths. More than 100,000 mu of fields in each embankment have been destroyed. Starving people are everywhere, a tragic sight beyond description. They are waiting for relief to prolong their lives. The association has allocated 5,000 yuan each for emergency relief in the Guangji Embankment and various embankments in Wuhu, and has remitted the funds to Mr. Ding and Director Zhai to expedite emergency relief. Furthermore, more than 20 counties in northern Anhui, including Su County, Fuyang, Yingshang, Si County, Wuhe, Linhuai, Fengtai, and Huaiyuan, central Anhui, including Hefei, Huoshan, and Quanjiao, and southern Anhui, including Wanzhi, Fanchang, and Dongliu, have suffered from severe floods or hailstorms, resulting in dire circumstances and unbearable suffering for the people. The disasters are severe, with only minor variations. They are sending telegrams and weeping, lamenting the impossibility of providing relief. The association has been providing relief for more than ten years, and the relief efforts have been particularly heavy in recent years, exhausting all resources and lacking the means to cook rice. The lives of the people are hanging by a thread, and their cries to heaven go unanswered. It is hoped that kind people and charitable organizations at home and abroad will offer help and donate generously. For example, the World Book Company generously made a vow to donate the full day's proceeds from book sales to help with relief, contributing more than 1,300 yuan to Anhui relief. Such initiatives will hopefully inspire others to contribute, and the dying disaster victims will have cause to celebrate their survival.

Two Anhui Charities Beg for Flood Relief 210

Letter to Xu Jingren

The Anqing Branch of the World Red Cross Society and the Anhui Provincial Private Charity Federation sent a letter to Mr. Xu Jingren on August 3rd: "Before the flames of war have died down, floods have struck again. The Guangji Embankment near our province and city suddenly collapsed after You Day, severing the lifeline of the people's food supply in several counties along the Yangtze River. The disaster area is hundreds of miles wide, directly affecting hundreds of thousands of people and indirectly affecting millions of people. The provincial capital and important cities along the river have seen businesses close and the population cease working. Boats travel on the thoroughfares, accompanied by fish and shrimp. Vegetables and other delicacies are now considered insignificant, and mountain fowl have become weeds. People are eating cattle to survive, caring only for the present and neglecting the future. The cries of starving people are everywhere, and rescue is difficult. Our two associations dispatched dozens of staff members the day after the disaster on You Day, traveling by boat in the rain to distribute pancakes and steamed buns, rotating daily to distribute dry food, totaling 60 million jin. The Provincial Government convened a meeting yesterday, passed regulations, and elected standing committee members. Before the Flood Relief Committee of the government is organized, the charitable organizations will continue to raise funds and distribute emergency relief to save the starving people. Therefore, in addition to entrusting Mr. Fu Shunsheng in Shanghai to make an appeal nearby, we have specifically designated Representative Wang Duzhai to bring ten copies of disaster photos and sincerely visit your residence to personally present the disaster situation and emergency relief measures. We know that you are a great philanthropist who is concerned about hunger and drowning and has compassion for the world. During this time of widespread catastrophe, it is time to spread your benevolence widely. We earnestly beg you to have pity on the suffering and provide early rescue. You can either send personnel from your organization to Anhui to distribute relief, or directly entrust our two associations to handle it. We await your instructions. With the utmost anticipation, the Anqing Branch of the World Red Cross Society and the Anhui Provincial Private Charity Federation. August 3rd."

A Candid Discussion on the Jiangning Flood Disaster 211

Mr. Leng Jun, the Magistrate of Jiangning County, was publicly recommended by the local community to come to Shanghai to raise relief funds. This was reported in a previous issue. Yesterday, our reporter visited him at his residence, and the following is a record of his conversation. The flood disaster in Jiangning this time is exceptionally severe, the worst seen in recent decades. Since the beginning of summer this year, there have been continuous wind and rain for weeks, causing mountain torrents and rivers to rise simultaneously. The water level has overflowed and there is no way to release it. On July 24th, from morning till evening, torrential rain poured down, and in an instant, the water depth on the flat ground reached several feet. Except for the 382nd district, which suffered less due to the mountainous terrain, almost all other districts in the county were turned into a watery expanse. Seventy to eighty percent of the large and small embankments were submerged and destroyed, and those that have not yet collapsed are in imminent danger. The loss of fields, houses, and livestock is countless. According to reports from district and township heads, the estimated area of affected farmland is over 400,000 mu, and the affected population is approximately 100,000. In addition to the three existing shelters, they are still insufficient to meet the urgent needs. The Beijing-Shanghai Railway line from Xiaguan to Yaohuamen is lined with flood victims on both sides. Some have built temporary shelters with straw mats, while others are temporarily staying on high ground, exposed to wind and dew, in a state of extreme misery. The county government has not only submitted requests to the provincial authorities for relief and participated in the capital's emergency relief efforts, but also publicly recommended representatives to come to Shanghai to raise donations. They have already contacted Ningbo gentlemen and major philanthropists in Shanghai, and the results have been quite satisfactory.

Inspection of Ningbo Ships Arriving with Epidemics 212

Remarks by Director Hu

Reliable reports from the seaport quarantine indicate that a small number of cholera cases have occurred in Yin County recently. The bureau has specially collaborated with the Municipal Health Bureau to implement inspections of passengers on Ningbo ships entering the port. The Municipal Health Bureau has dispatched quarantine doctors to conduct inspections. Yesterday, a reporter from the Guowen News Agency visited the bureau director, Mr. Hu Hongji, to inquire about the current situation of quarantine. He replied as follows:

Quarantine of Ningbo Ships Mr. Hu stated that during the period when seasonal epidemics are about to occur, all major ports around the world have health authorities established by their respective countries' major cities, which dispatch permanent doctors to designated sea lines where ships anchor before entering the port. The quarantine doctors thoroughly examine the physical condition of all passengers on board for any signs of infectious diseases. At the same time, stool samples are collected from each passenger. Only those whose stool samples are found to be free of infectious bacteria are allowed to disembark. For example, when Japanese ships enter Nagasaki, the local health authorities' quarantine work is meticulous and often continues day and night, with some inspections taking more than a day. Shanghai is a place with a diverse population and dense population. Cholera is rampant every year, and the number of deaths is alarming. To prevent problems before they occur, the bureau's work during this year's cholera prevention period is more active than in previous years. After all, when an epidemic breaks out in a major city in any country, it directly creates a continuous link with the international community. Since the true cholera disease occurred in Ningbo, the bureau immediately implemented inspections of Ningbo ships entering the port after receiving the report. This started on August 1st. However, the shipping industry initially had requests due to business hours. The bureau also provided special convenience to shipping companies in the quarantine procedures. When Ningbo ships arrive at Songkou at 4:00 AM every morning, the bureau's six doctors stationed in Wusong take small boats to the ships when they display the signal lights (i.e., three red lights) to conduct quarantine and administer vaccinations, as well as test stool samples. It takes one to two hours from Songkou to the dock where the ships stop at the Bund, and the doctors' quarantine and vaccinations also take only three to four hours. Therefore, there is actually no impact on the shipping companies' business. The results of the inspections in recent days have been good. True cholera has rarely been found among the passengers. However, all passengers must be forcibly injected with preventive vaccines by the doctors.

Vaccination Work August 1st was the first day of implementing quarantine for Ningbo ships entering the port. However, because the port companies of each ship had not notified the ship captains in advance, the doctors sent by the Municipal Health Bureau on the first day did not receive a formal inspection. When the Taikoo Xinjing Beijing ship entered the port on the second day, 760 people were vaccinated and 14 stool samples were checked. On the Ningshao ship, 520 people were vaccinated and 10 stool samples were checked. There were no sailings on the third day. On the fourth day, 600 people were vaccinated on the Xinjiang Tian ship and 10 stool samples were checked. Approximately 1,000 people were vaccinated on the Ningxing ship and 15 stool samples were checked. On the fifth day, 600 people were vaccinated on the New Beijing ship and 18 stool samples were checked. 600 people were vaccinated on the Xin Ning Shao ship and 14 stool samples were checked. On the sixth day, 600 people were vaccinated on the Xinjiang Tian ship and 21 stool samples were checked. 640 people were vaccinated on the Ningxing ship and 20 stool samples were checked. These are the approximate figures for vaccinations and stool sample inspections in recent days, but fortunately, no cholera patients have entered the port.

Establishment of the Shanghai Silk Industry Bank 215

Authorized Capital of 600,000 Yuan

Board of Directors and Supervisors Elected

In March of this year, leaders in the silk industry and prominent figures in the financial world in this city jointly initiated the organization of a Silk Industry Bank, with the aim of regulating finance and benefiting society. The original capital of the bank was set at 500,000 yuan. However, due to the enthusiastic subscription of shares by various silk industry groups and the warm support from all sectors, the number of subscribed shares exceeded the fixed amount, so it was revised to 600,000 yuan. All preparatory matters have been completed, and the share capital has also been fully paid up. The bank held a shareholders' founding meeting at the City Chamber of Commerce at 2:00 PM on the 5th of this month. The articles of association were passed on the spot, and Wang Yansong, Pan Gongzhan, Jiang Linshu, Lu Zhengbing, Zhang Danru, Pei Yunqing, Feng Zhongqing, Hu Xisheng, Shen Qinzhai, Yu Guozhen, and Chen Ziming were elected as directors. Xu Jiqing, Jin Jianqing, and Cheng Yongliu were elected as supervisors. It is reported that the bank is currently submitting its application to the Ministry to complete the registration procedures and will be able to start business soon.

Lawsuit for the Collision of the Xinkang Ship 216

The Special District Court Schedules a Hearing

The case of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Xinkang ship being sunk by the Japanese ship Ryuyo Maru has been going on for more than two years, with no progress in the negotiations. The dead are drowned at the bottom of the sea, and the living are in pain. Continuing to delay this matter is not a way to comfort the dead and reassure the living. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company had already filed a lawsuit for damages with the Shanghai Special District Court. Several summonses have been issued, but because the other party has not arrived, the case has not progressed. All the families of the victims have also entrusted lawyers Wu Jingxiong and Sheng Zhenwei to file a petition with the court, requesting a judgment ordering compensation for damages, totaling 1,110,862.27 national currency, and bearing the litigation costs. After the court received the petition, considering the importance of the matter, it has now scheduled a hearing for the morning of the 15th of this month.

Huang Haiqing 217

Stabbed to Death with Multiple Knives 218

Revenge Killing? ... Murder?

At 6:45 AM yesterday morning, a man was stabbed to death with multiple knives at the entrance of Xicheng Lane on Avenue Ruì Brénier, French Concession. The details are as follows:

Tragic Cry for Help At 6:30 AM yesterday morning, residents near Xicheng Lane were still sound asleep when they suddenly heard a tragic cry for help. They got out of bed to watch and saw the deceased lying diagonally at the entrance of the lane. The four murderers fled towards Avenue Lafayette and through Xicheng Lane towards Avenue Foch, leaving no trace. At that time, a growing number of onlookers gathered. The patrol station on Songshan Road was notified and immediately led patrols to investigate. The deceased was wearing a white silk long gown, with a white cotton short shirt and trousers underneath, black socks and black shoes, and the soft-brimmed straw hat he was wearing on his head had been thrown at the entrance of the lane. Blood was all over the ground. It was counted that there was one knife wound on his back, which was pulled out by the patrolmen afterwards, one knife wound on his chest, and one knife wound on each side of his waist. He was immediately taken by car to the coroner's office.

Eyewitness Account According to eyewitnesses, the deceased left the lane alone at around 6:30 AM yesterday morning and hired a rickshaw to the North Railway Station, agreeing on the fare. Just as he was about to get into the rickshaw, four people resembling workers suddenly rushed out from behind the deceased, each taking out a sharp knife. They first stabbed the deceased severely in the back with a knife, which went deep into the flesh, and then stabbed him in the chest, which the deceased pulled out himself. He was stabbed in each side of the waist, and blood gushed out. The deceased died instantly. The murderers fled in southwest directions.

Family Report At that time, many people gathered to watch, and the deceased's eldest son, Daquan, also learned that there was news of a pedestrian being stabbed to death at the entrance of the lane. He ran out to watch and, upon seeing that it was his father, turned back to inform his mother and blew a whistle madly. As the number of onlookers increased, the deceased's wife, Jin, and concubine, Chen, arrived and mourned over the body. According to the deceased's wife, Yao, the deceased's surname was Huang, named Haiqing, 38 years old, from Wuwei County, Anhui Province, formerly residing at No. 8 Fengyu Lane on Avenue Foch, and recently moved to No. 54 Xicheng Lane for only two months. The deceased previously worked as a gatekeeper patrolman at the baseball field on Avenue de l'Observatoire in the French Concession. He was dismissed nearly three years ago. He also opened the Changjiang Public Apartment on Caishi Road in the Caishi Fang the year before, but closed it down last spring, so his finances were extremely tight. He had just taken up the position of squad leader of the fourth district detective team of the Wusong Jiangsu Provincial Maritime Public Security Team five days ago, but had not yet reported for duty. Therefore, he took a car to the Wusong district headquarters to report for duty this morning, but unexpectedly he was brutally murdered by bandits as soon as he left his house.

Huang Haiqing's Portrait 219

Court Examination The patrol station reported to the Second Court of the Special District, and Prosecutor Ding Shikui was appointed to examine the body at the coroner's office at 10:00 AM, accompanied by a clerk and a forensic doctor. He took his seat in court. The detective reported the previous situation and presented the two murder weapons to the court. After Mr. Ding questioned the deceased's wife, Huang Jin, he ruled that the deceased Huang Haiqing had indeed been stabbed to death before his death, and allowed the deceased's wife to sign a certificate to claim the body for coffining and burial, pending the patrol station's arrest of the murderer for investigation. After the examination, the patrol station took photos of the body, and the family members collected it in the afternoon.

The Condition of the Deceased's Family The deceased had one wife and one concubine, who lived together in a two-story building at No. 54 Xicheng Lane. The wife lived in the front building and the concubine lived in the back building. The wife, Jin, 36 years old, had three sons: the eldest, Dajin, 14 years old; the second, Sanbaozi, 9 years old; and the third, Laobazi, 5 years old. The concubine, Chen, 37 years old, had been with Huang for eight years and currently works as a nanny in a foreigner's home. She gave birth to twin sons a week ago, but one died young, and the other was named Shuangzi. The deceased's older brother, Huang Youshu, 48 years old, works at the Longhua Ordnance Pharmaceutical Factory and also lives with his younger brother and his family, relying entirely on the deceased for survival. Now that he has tragically fallen victim to bandits, the future is worrying.

Post-Incident Investigation According to friends of the deceased, the deceased was strong-willed and never showed mercy when handling official affairs, which often incurred the hatred of bandits. This brutal murder may have been carried out by bandits seeking revenge. According to neighbors of the deceased, the deceased had an affair with a woman surnamed [Omitted] and even caused a storm of jealousy. This murder may also be a case of adultery.

Wang Zengshou, Who Embezzled 200,000 Yuan,

Apprehended 220

Accomplice Shi Wenhao Flees to Japan

Taichang Qianzhuang Sends Telegram Requesting Arrest

In January of this year, Shi Wenhao, a partner, and Wang Zengshou, an accountant, of Ruyi Lane's Taichang Qianzhuang colluded to embezzle a huge sum of 200,000 yuan and fled without a trace. After the associate manager of the qianzhuang noticed this, he immediately ordered other partners to check the accounts, reported it to the patrol station for arrest, and requested lawyer Jiang Yiping to represent him in posting a notice in various newspapers in Shanghai, offering a reward of 10,000 yuan for the arrest. However, after the notice was posted for a long time, there was still no trace of them. Later, at the request of Wang Zengshou's relatives and friends, the reward for the arrest was canceled in order to find them. The qianzhuang complied and requested the patrol station to cancel the reward and arrest order. Lawyer Jiang was then asked to post a notice in the newspaper canceling the arrest and reward. It was hoped that Shi and Wang would send someone to mediate and arrange things, but unexpectedly, half a year passed and there was still no news. Therefore, a report was filed with various neighboring district and inland government offices to try to capture them. The day before yesterday, the Public Security Bureau of Dachang Town sent police to Shanghai to report to the qianzhuang that the fugitive Wang Zengshou had already been arrested in Dachang. According to his confession, the accomplice Shi Wenhao fled to Japan after the incident, while he himself could not leave because he had family. After Manager Luo of the qianzhuang heard the news, he rushed to the Dachang Public Security Bureau that night and requested that the case be transferred to the Special District Court of the Public Concession for trial. He also sent a secret telegram to the Japanese authorities, requesting that Shi Wenhao be arrested and brought back for interrogation.

A Wealthy Family from Xiaoshan Kidnapped

Contact Planned in Shanghai 221

Negotiations at the Entrance of the Quelou Hotel

Chen Xuewen, Zhou Luren, et al., Arrested

Wang Guisheng, a wealthy family from Dayi, Xiaoshan County, Shaoxing, was kidnapped by bandits on the 23rd of last month. Later, his family received more than ten letters from the bandits, demanding a ransom of 52,000 yuan. The last letter instructed the Wang family to send someone to open a room at the Quelou Hotel on Xizang Road in Shanghai on August 4th, with the name Wang Jianyi written on the room card. The person should carry one hat box from the Hangzhou Zhang Yun Sheng Hat Shop, one large and one small, and someone would come to contact them. After receiving the letter, the Wang family reported it to the Hangzhou Public Security Bureau, which ordered detective team leader Zhu Xiaodong and deputy team leader He Yongfu to come to Shanghai. They filed a report with the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, and Director Chen assigned detective Gao Wansheng to report to the Old Gate Patrol Station. The patrol head ordered detectives Xu Zexin and Feng Xiushan to go to the Quelou Hotel and open rooms 75 and 76, following the instructions in the bandit's letter. At 5:15 PM the day before yesterday, the detectives received a phone call from the bandits, instructing the Wang family representative to come down to the hotel entrance for negotiations. The Hangzhou detective Qi Yunjian pretended to be the representative and waited at the hotel entrance, while the other detectives were scattered around in ambush. Before long, Chen Xuewen and Zhou Luren, both from Shaoxing, came to talk to Qi and were arrested. At that time, there was also a Shanghai man named Cao Jinsheng, who was arrested after the detectives suspected his behavior. They were all taken to the patrol station and detained. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the First Criminal Division of the Special District Court. The patrol station's lawyer, Ru Baoyi, stated that Chen and Zhou had just arrived in Shanghai two days ago, which showed that their trip was purely for the purpose of negotiating the ransom. Cao Jinsheng was a chauffeur who had dropped off his master, Wang Shanzhi, at Yipinxian and then got out of the car to play. He did not know how he had been arrested for suspicious behavior. After investigation, it was found that he was not involved and should be released. The Public Security Bureau requested to transfer Chen and Zhou, and the patrol station did not object. Presiding Judge Zhou Hanting verified the report and questioned the three defendants. He then ruled that Chen Xuewen and Zhou Luren be handed over to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for transfer to the Hangzhou Public Security Bureau for investigation. Cao Jinsheng was released on bail of 500 yuan.

Two Bandit Leaders Sentenced to Death

Qian Weizhu Sentenced to Fifteen Years

Xu and Sun Sentenced to Eight Years Each

Yang Aquan, a Chinese detective, and Shen Yuzhou and Liu Changgen, detectives from the Yangshupu Patrol Station, previously arrested Wang Zhenji, Wei Yuzhai, Qian Weizhu, Xu Guozhu, Sun Hongshun, Zhang Kejin, Zhang Han, Yang Chen, and suspects Qian Weizhong and Qian Shen, all from Jiangbei, and confiscated two pistols and seven bullets. It was found that between February and June of this year, they used firearms to rob Weng Dachu at No. 1384 Dongyangshupu Road and opened fire to harm Indian patrolmen Kena Xing and Xu Guisheng at an unnumbered address on Qiqihaer Road, as well as Zhang Wang, a woman on Dagu Road, of clothing, jewelry, and silver worth more than 200 yuan. Wang Zhenji, Dong Yuzhai, and Qian Weizhu also attempted to kidnap Chen Bingxiang, a Cantonese, on Morrison Road at 9:00 PM on June 17, but he escaped. The patrol station sent the suspects to the First Court of the Special District. After the interrogation was completed, Presiding Judge Feng Shide took his seat in the Third Court yesterday morning and sentenced Wang Zhenji and Dong Yuzhai to death, Qian Weizhu to fifteen years in prison, and Xu Guozhu and Sun Hongshun to eight years in prison each. Zhang Kejin and Zhang Han were each sentenced to three months in prison, and Yang Chen was sentenced to two months in prison. The number of days of detention before the judgment was determined to be equivalent to one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention. The two pistols and seven bullets were confiscated. Qian Weizhong and Qian Shen were found not guilty. Sun Hongshun had committed other crimes in the French Concession and was sent back to that court for execution after the sentence was carried out. The clothing of the deceased Chen San was stored in the warehouse.

Three Men and One Woman Die Tragically 222

Automobile Pleasure Cruise Yang Cheng Biao, 24, from Tongzhou, a ticket seller at the Tianchan Theater, was the nephew of Gu Zhuxuan. Yesterday morning at 4:00 AM, he and three friends hired a chauffeur-driven car and went for a pleasure cruise in the Wusong area. Before they were far from their destination, when the car was turning, it collided with a telephone pole on the side of the road because it was going too fast. With a loud bang, the car was smashed to pieces. Yang and his friend Lu Xiugui jumped out of the car, but Lu only suffered minor injuries to his face and hands. However, Yang Cheng Biao's brain was splattered and his breath was weak. His friends immediately hired a car and rushed him to the Tongren Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective. He died around 7:00 AM.

Touching Electrical Wire While Washing Hands Donghai Cinema, at Tilanqiao, invited the famous "Tang Fei" of the Shenjiawan Fire Brigade to perform "Immortal Carrying" and various martial arts last night. Ah Cai, a coppersmith from the fire brigade, about 30 years old, went to help out. Because his hands were dirty, he saw a jar of water on the ground backstage and bent down to wash them. Unexpectedly, there was electricity in the water, and he touched it with both hands, and died on the spot. He was taken to the Tongren Hospital and transferred to the coroner's office by fire engine, pending a court examination.

Poor Swimming Skills Yu Shuanglin, 30, a worker at the Xiangtai Lumber Company in Yangshupu, went to the Lan Road River to take a cold bath the night before. Unfortunately, he was not good at swimming and drowned. It was not until about 5:00 PM yesterday afternoon that the body floated to the surface of the water. A pedestrian saw it and called a Chinese patrolman from No. 2624 to come and retrieve the body. It was taken to the Tongren Hospital and transferred to the Fielun Road coroner's office for examination.

Falling from a Height A woman named Yang Ada, 12, from Anhui Province, was employed as a maid by a family at No. 210 Avenue Foch in the French Concession. At 10:40 AM yesterday morning, she was playing with her young master on the balcony when she accidentally fell and died from her injuries. The owner immediately took the child's body to the Renji Hospital and reported it to the patrol station. Bao Tan Wang Licheng was ordered to go to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall to report to the Second Special District Court for examination.

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau Plans to

Establish a Poor People's Loan in the Public Concession 223

Depending on Whether It Can Get Assistance from the Public Works Department

There are many poor people in this city, and it is difficult for them to make a living. They suffer greatly from high-interest loans (such as "printing money"). Since the municipal government established poor people's loan offices in Nanshi and Zhabei, the poor people in the north and south cities have been able to gradually eliminate the oppression of high-interest loans. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau is in charge of this matter. Recently, it has produced hundreds of porcelain-enameled loan notices and distributed them to Nanshi trams and public buses in the north and south cities, so that the poor can know that there are places to borrow money and will no longer have to borrow printing money. In view of recent reports of Indians and a few Chinese people lending printing money in the concession and committing various cruel and brutal acts, it is eager to promote poor people's loans in the concession to alleviate the suffering of the poor. However, the situation in the concession is special and difficult to handle. Unless it can get the sincere assistance of the Public Works Department and its affiliated agencies, it will be difficult to do so. Therefore, the Social Affairs Bureau sent a letter to the Public Works Department of the Public Concession, which said:

"It has been reported that Indians and a small number of Chinese people are lending printing money in the concession, which is cruel. This Bureau cannot help but feel sad. Since the city established the first and second loan offices in Nanshi and Zhabei, the poor people in those areas have rarely suffered from borrowing printing money. The poor people in the concession are also our Chinese citizens, and we should treat them equally. Now, in order to help the poor, the poor people living in the Public Concession can also borrow money from the first and second poor people's loan offices in this city, according to the regulations of the poor people's loan offices in this city. However, the prerequisite is whether it can get the sincere cooperation and assistance of your bureau and its affiliated agencies. For example, in order to prove the household registration of the borrower and to track down the absconding borrowers, this city has the assistance of the various district offices of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. The investigators of the loan office also need the assistance and protection of the local police when they go out to fulfill their duties. If your bureau and its affiliated agencies can provide the same assistance as the Municipal Public Security Bureau, this Bureau will send personnel to your bureau to discuss the detailed implementation plan as soon as a reply is received, in order to benefit the poor people. Attached is a copy of the second collection of the Bureau's laws and regulations, in which the regulations of the poor people's loan offices are on page 99. Please check it."

If the Public Works Department can assist, the poor people in the concession can also slightly alleviate the suffering of their lives.

The Last Day of the French Court Hearing the Case of Reconciliation 224

The Case of Maintenance Between Wu Li and Wu Shujun

Wu Li, a young woman from Ningbo, previously hired lawyer Jin Yu to file a complaint with the former Shanghai French Public Court, accusing her husband, Wu Shujun, of abandonment and failure to provide maintenance, requesting a judgment granting her living expenses of 20,000 yuan. The court approved the complaint and ordered a summons. Presiding Judge Zhu adjudicated the case on the last day of his term. Wu Li continued to hire lawyer Jin to file a lawsuit with the Second District Court of the Special District. The defendant's lawyer, Yue Junfen, came forward to mediate and had discussed a peaceful settlement with the plaintiff's lawyer. After repeated negotiations, a decision was made to settle the case for 5,000 yuan. At about 2:00 PM yesterday, the lawyers from both sides invited the plaintiffs, defendants, relatives, and friends to the scene to write and sign a settlement agreement. The case of a husband and wife involved in litigation thus came to an end.

Regarding the case of armed clashes between two gangs of Hubei workers from the Xiexing Public Company and Anlu Hostel in Pudong over the competition for cargo transportation business at Hongsheng Wharf, it is understood that Jiang Hanrong and Gao Lin, two severely injured workers from Anlu Hostel, are still in the hospital and have not fully recovered. Riding with Dance Hostess Leads to Disaster 227

Car Crashes into Big Tree

Dance Hostess Injured in Head

Pan Deping, an employee of the Universal Savings Society, is a young and handsome gentleman who often goes to various dance halls during his spare time to do the foxtrot. Therefore, he is often seen at the gates of the Moon Palace and Great East dance halls. The night before, Pan went to the Great East dance hall and danced with Ren Qiuyue, a dance hostess from Suzhou (16 years old, living at No. 2, Alley 1, Daqing Lane, Great Horse Road). When they became bored at around 3 a.m. the next morning, they went on a suburban tour with Ren Qiuyue and another dance hostess, Lu Xiaomei (17 years old, from Suzhou). They hired a No. 7624 covered truck from a certain car dealership at No. 72 Guangxi Road, driven by the driver Ma Fuzhen, and asked him to drive them around the western suburbs of Shanghai. Because it was late at night and there were few pedestrians, Ma stepped on the gas pedal, driving at full speed, with the semblance of soaring through the clouds. Unexpectedly, misfortune is unpredictable. When the car arrived at the intersection of Fuxu Road and Seymour Road, it crashed into a big tree by the roadside with a screech. The bumper and headlights of the car were severely damaged. Ren Qiuyue injured her head, but the others were unharmed. Afterwards, she was taken to Baolong Hospital for treatment by car.

Scrap Copper Injures Two People 228

At 8:20 PM last night, Zhu Youde, Guo Zhongxin, and Feng Shouming, employees of Demao Copper Shop at No. 25 Luxiangyuan Road in the city, were ordered by the shop owner Feng Guolin to inspect the old scrap copper they had collected for melting. Unexpectedly, there were explosive objects mixed in the old copper. After being struck violently, it exploded with a loud noise and sparks flew in all directions. Neighbors on the left and right came to look upon hearing the sound and saw that the coppersmiths Guo Zhongxin and Feng Shouming had been injured in the arms by copper fragments and had fainted on the ground. Then the police arrived and detained Zhu Youde at the First Sub-station of the Second District for investigation. The injured coppersmiths Guo and Feng were sent to the hospital for treatment by the shop.

White Porcelain House Number Cannot Be Made Yourself 229

Xiao Yunlu, a native of Hunan, recently opened the Beihai Chun Restaurant at No. 113 in Jiumu Di. Because he hung up signs everywhere, he covered up the porcelain house number nailed up by the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau. Later, Xiao heard from others that the house number could not be obscured, lest he be fined. Thereupon, Xiao privately made a piece of No. 113 house number with lead skin and white paint and nailed it to the door. It was spotted by patrolman Chen Lirong, who took Xiao to the First Sub-station of the Second District for violating the police regulations after prying off the privately made house number. After questioning, Xu, the chief of the sub-station, found that Xiao Yunlu's private manufacture of the house number was due to a misunderstanding of what people said. Therefore, he was given a light fine and dismissed.

Pretending to Sell Cigarettes and Robbing Money 230

Chen Decai and Wang Keming Arrested

Recently, a type of robber has been discovered in the city. They specialize in pretending to sell counterfeit cigarettes in various streets and alleys. When ordinary pedestrians stop to watch, these people will squeeze the viewers and search for money. At about 7 AM yesterday, Gu Baoru, a native of Wuxi who worked at the Ningyi Public Customs Brokerage at No. 28 Yongan Lane, Yongan Street in the French Concession, was carrying more than 200 yuan in paper money to the south, intending to go to the Dasheng Storage at Shengyi Wharf to pick up goods. Unexpectedly, when he arrived at Shengyi Wharf, a stranger holding a cigarette came forward and said, "Sir, please try this cigarette. It is the latest product. This product has good tobacco and the price is right. Please try it, and you will know that I am not lying." At that time, another accomplice immediately stepped forward and lit a lighter to invite Gu to smoke. Upon seeing this, Gu immediately stopped and stared blankly. Suddenly, two more bandits came up from behind, taking advantage of Gu's unpreparedness, and squeezed Gu in an attempt to search for money. Gu, knowing that he was being robbed, desperately broke free and ran to Yuan Huirong, the police officer at the Dasheng Storage of the First Sub-station of the First District, to report. Yuan Huirong rushed to the scene and arrested the two bandits who were pretending to sell cigarettes and took them back to the sub-station. During the preliminary trial by the chief of the sub-station, Gu recounted the whole story and requested that they be punished. Questioned, the two criminals confessed their names as Chen Decai, 31 years old, from Yancheng, residing in a certain inn on Taiping Bridge, and Wang Keming, 34 years old, from Yuyao, and both claimed to make a living selling cigarettes. The rest of their confessions were vague. They were ordered to prepare a document and send it to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

A Man Jumps into the Huangpu River and Dies 231

At about 10 p.m. on the 2nd of this month, a man dressed in blue cloth pants, naked on his upper body, and resembling a coolie suddenly came to the Dongjiadu Wharf in Nanshi. Taking advantage of people's lack of preparation, he jumped into the Huangpu River. Upon hearing the sound, boatmen rushed to the scene to rescue him. However, it was dark at the time, and the man was not seen emerging for a long time after entering the water, so the rescue was unsuccessful. Spectators all said that he must have been buried in the belly of a fish and sighed in succession. Unexpectedly, the corpse suddenly emerged when the long-distance bus ferry from Shangnan arrived at the port the day before yesterday. After being reported to the Nanshi Wharf Lifesaving Bureau, the corpse was taken back and coffined and placed in a hall for identification.

Hu Baogen Approved for Transfer 232

On the 3rd of this month, Xue Renquan, a detective from the Changzhou Public Security Bureau, and Cao Xirong, a Chinese detective from the Huishan Police Station, arrested Hu Baogen, alias Sheng Baida, a bandit from Changzhou, at the Kunming Inn on Kunming Road. Because he committed a crime in his original籍, the First Court of the Special Zone ordered that the Wujin County Government submit evidence for further verification. The defendant was taken into custody. Yesterday morning, Zhao Xilin, a detective from the Wujin County Government, delivered a letter to the Third Criminal Court of the Special Court, stating that the defendant's residence in his original籍 was not far from mine, and there was no doubt that Sheng Baida was Hu Baogen. In the past, he had gone to his home twice to arrest him but failed, etc. When questioned, Hu Baogen also admitted that his alias was Sheng Baida, but he did not know about the bandit case in his original籍. Li Zhishan, a lawyer from the police station, expressed his agreement to the transfer of the defendant. After being verified and reported by Judge Tao Bingrong, it was ordered that Hu Baogen, alias Sheng Baida, be handed over to Yang Xilin, a detective from the Wujin County Government, to be taken back to his original籍 for trial.

Ye Garden to Open Soon 233

Reception for the Press Yesterday Afternoon

Ye Garden in Jiangwan, with its clear waters and lush trees, is a charming landscape, covering an area of more than 70 acres. It is a famous garden in Shanghai, which is usually not open to the public. Only with the introduction of acquaintances can one enter for sightseeing. Now, Zhuo Da Wu, Zhou Shenjin, Jin Yong, and others have organized the Tongqing Company to rent this excellent garden from the owner, to share with the people of Shanghai. It will open soon. On the basis of the original beautiful scenery of the garden, more upscale entertainment will be added, such as dancing, movies, mini golf, boating, and ball games, all of which are available. Yesterday afternoon, Zhuo, Zhou, and Jin specially held a banquet to invite members of the press to visit. More than 40 people attended, and were received by Feng Zhaoliang, Li Heyun, and others. They dispersed in joy at 4 p.m. As soon as the garden is fully decorated, it will be open to the public.

Silk Factories Change to Half-Day Work Due to Hot Weather 237

The silk factory industry in this port is experiencing abnormal heat. The temperature in the workshops has increased sharply. The female workers are sweating like rain. Therefore, the silk factories that have started work have all temporarily suspended their summer vacation from the day before yesterday, and reduced their work to half a day in the morning, starting work at 6:30 a.m. and ending work at 1:30 p.m. Work is stopped in the afternoon. The original state will be restored when the weather cools down.

The World Bookstore was founded in the 10th year of the Republic of China and will be celebrating its 10th anniversary. A commemorative gift coupon event will be held for two months starting from August 10th. The details of the gift coupon event and the general situation of the bookstore have been obtained below. (Gift Coupon) From August 10th to October 9th, during these two months, for every five jiao of the bookstore's original edition books purchased, a book coupon worth one jiao will be given; for every one yuan, a book coupon worth two jiao will be given, and so on. For every one yuan spent on stationery, instruments, consignment books, and magazine subscriptions, a book coupon worth one jiao will be given, and so on. (Capital) The initial capital was only 15,000 yuan, but due to business development, it has increased over the years, and the current paid-up capital is more than 660,000 yuan. (Organization) In addition to the board of directors, the management consists of the General Affairs Office, the Editorial Office, the Printing Office, and the Distribution Office, four major departments, which are further divided into various departments and sections, led by the general manager. (Property) In the 14th year of the Republic of China, the bookstore purchased more than ten mu of land in Dalianwan Road in this port and built more than sixty factory buildings. This year, a new four-story office building was built. In the 18th year, the site of the general distribution office on Sima Road was purchased, and a seven-story building is currently being planned. In addition, branch offices in Guangzhou, Changsha, Nanchang, Wuhu and other places have been purchased. The bookstore's assets have reached more than 2 million yuan. (Branches) The bookstore has its own branches in important commercial ports and provincial capitals, such as Guangzhou, Shantou, Wuzhou, Xiamen, Hangzhou, Nanjing, Jinan, Tianjin, Beiping, Shenyang, Taiyuan, Hankou, Changsha, Chongqing, Nanchang, Wuhu, and other more than twenty places. News from Trade Associations 248

Zhejiang Cocoon Industry: The preparatory committee of the Joint Association of Zhejiang Cocoon Industry Associations held its fifth preparatory meeting at 3 p.m. the other day, at the Shanghai office of Lianzhuli, Aiwuyi Road. Those present were Chu Huiseng, Jiang Laixian, Chen Jingxian, Shen Tianbi, Zhang Youyi, Wang Lucui, Chen Menghui, Yu Songqing, Wang Lianfang, Zhang Ximin, Yu Wenhai, Shi Zusheng, Yu Xingshu, Chen Weixuan, etc. The meeting was held as usual. Shen Tiancui was elected as the chairman. The following matters were resolved: 1. It was resolved that the date of the general meeting was set for September 6, and the formal establishment meeting would be held in Hangzhou at the Zhejiang Provincial Chamber of Commerce Joint Association. The reception office was set up at the Hangzhou City Station Hotel. 2. It was resolved to submit a request to the Provincial Party Department and send a letter to the Provincial Chamber of Commerce Joint Association, requesting them to send personnel for guidance. 3. Election rules: Shen Tianxin and Chen Jingxian were elected to draft the election rules. The election principle was that the association would be the unit for electors, and the representative would be the limit for those being elected. 4. It was resolved that Chen Jingxian would be elected to draft the written request to exempt cocoon business tax, which would be submitted for approval at the general meeting. 5. It was resolved that the membership cards would be prepared by the association itself, and the ballots would be issued by the Provincial Party Department. 6. It was resolved that the draft of the association's charter would be amended in accordance with the Commercial Association Law in Article 13, as instructed by the Provincial Party Department. It was resolved that in addition to complying with the amendment, Article 21 would be resolved and stipulated by the general meeting and then reported. 7. It was resolved that 200 copies of the draft charter of the association would be printed. 8. It was resolved that there were 12 associations that had reported the attendance of representatives. Those who had not reported were resolved to be contacted separately. 9. It was resolved that the announcement would be published in Shen and Xin two newspapers for two days each, and in the two Hangzhou newspapers for three days each, one month before the date of the general meeting. 10. It was resolved to send membership cards to the associations and to notify them of the date and location of the establishment meeting and to attach the draft charter and the minutes of this meeting.

Rubber Industry: The National Rubber Products Industry Association held the inauguration ceremony of the first executive and supervisory committee at its clubhouse on Aiduya Road yesterday. Feng Yunchu was publicly elected as the chairman and the ceremony was held as usual. The members took the oath of office. The standing committee members were then elected by mutual election. As a result, Xue Fuji, Yang Yongnian, Shi Zhishan, Mao Yuheng, and Shen Mengshi were elected. The following cases were discussed: (1) It was resolved to pass the case that the products of rubber factories set up by Japanese in China should be boycotted by the Anti-Japanese Association as a whole. (2) It was resolved to pass the case that members' trademarks should be jointly published in advertisements to facilitate domestic purchases. (3) It was resolved to pass the case that the necessary Japanese raw materials for each factory should be registered with the Municipal Chamber of Commerce in accordance with the law. (4) It was resolved to pass the case that unscrupulous merchants who pass off Japanese factory products as domestic products should be strictly investigated in order to find ways to ban them. (5) It was resolved to pass the case that a design committee should be organized to design and manufacture necessary raw materials in order to permanently resist them. It was handed over to the Standing Committee to formulate a plan. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Laundry Industry: The Laundry Industry Association held its 35th Executive Committee meeting yesterday, with Tang Hengshan as the chairman. The following cases were discussed: (1) A letter from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce regarding the case that state-owned industries and state-run enterprises should be insured by Chinese companies in order to recover the rights and interests. It was resolved to file it. (2) A letter from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce regarding the case that during the boycott of Japanese goods, the price increase of national goods should be restricted in order to benefit the people, and instructed to inform and comply. It was resolved to notify the members. (3) According to the newspaper, the washing and dyeing industry's camp tax is listed as 2/1000. It is found that the industry specializes in washing white clothes, and each piece is only one or two cents, with very little profit. At present, they are all workers who make a living. It should not be taxed in the same way as the dyeing industry. It should be requested from the Finance Bureau to reduce the tax rate and list it as 1/1000. It was resolved to send a letter to the Tax Rules Research Association, requesting to reduce the tax. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Letter 251

To the esteemed editor: I am writing to you today to address a matter concerning the report in the Shanghai News section of the Shen Bao on the 5th, regarding the reorganization of the Wusong Water Police and the issuance of fishing boat flag licenses. The report stated that the Fourth District Headquarters hired a boat and sent personnel to implement inspections, but the flag license fee collected was more than ten times the prescribed amount, and even additional demands were made, causing great suffering to the boatmen. Reading this, I was greatly shocked. It has been verified that the issuance of fishing boat flag licenses was requested to the provincial government by the Wusong Chamber of Commerce and various boat gangs on their own initiative, not by the Fourth District of the Water Police proactively. After the district was ordered by the provincial government to investigate and reply for approval, the district chief set off to suppress bandits. All registration and fee collection procedures were handled by Yuan Xichou, the former section chief of the First Section, together with Mr. Zheng Shushan of the Wusong Chamber of Commerce. In addition to collecting the prescribed labor and flag license fees, the district headquarters was not involved in any other extra charges. I am afraid that this will mislead the audience, so I am writing to your newspaper to correct the situation. With best regards, Yours sincerely, Huang Wenhan, Accountant of the Fourth District of the former Provincial Water Police Team, August 6th.
